<UserId.>114850685248772040474</UserId.>< name>
Paul Hellemn< /name>
<Date>1571616977922</Date><Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
Really good selection and salad bar. All they have is falafel, in bowls or in pita sandwiches. The good part is the bar of cooked chickpeas, carrots, cabbage salad, pickles, cheese, peanuts, roasted eggplant etc that you can choose to fill out your bowl or sandwich with. You can take as much as you want. Even extra falafel is on the bar if you want. It's easy to get a good variety and to feel really healthy here.

If you're looking for a more simple falafel experience, then falafel boy around the corner has imo slightly better falafel. Their rice bowls are standard rice, falafel, some onion and tomato. I usually come to Liba for the better salad bar selection though, even though I think the falafel itself is better around the corner.</Text>

This place is rad! I was wandering around in search of pseudo-healthy lunch options and found Liba. I ordered a falafel salad; they handed me a good size (compostable) bowl and just pointed me to the salad bar.

<user_name>R W< /user_name><date>1447359739353</date><rating>5</rating><Review>Really good sweet potato fries with garlic, yummy falafel and 'falafel bar' to add fillings (the shaved brussel sprout salad and pickles were probably my favorite 2 toppings). <Resp>None< /Resp>< Text>
How do you get falafel haters or those unknown to the falafel and turn them into falafel lovers? Introduce them to Liba Falafel.

I was walking down 17th thinking of what to eat and the smell of Liba's kitchen caught my nose. My only experience with falafel was in college with dining common falafels and a restaurant down the road. . . in sum I was turned off by falafels. I started to think falafels was a food trend. Boy was I freaking WRONG.

I bought a Lotta Love Falafel sandwich which comes with sweet potato fries; a total of $13.13. They give you the pita with the falafel and you go to the salad bar to get your fixings on, I usually put the cucumber and  cabbage with herb dressing, some greens, feta cheese, and this fried pickled red onion topping. . . oh and a very generous amount of their yogurt sauce. Yes, yes, and YES!!! Love how it comes down to my own customization of my sandwich, more hands on approach.

The falafel really blew my mind,  the falafel trend does exist!! So crispy and flavorful, not dry compared to the others I tried. Then having it with their sweet potato fries was like flavor overload. The fries is garlic-cilantro-lime fries and even me typing all of it made my mouth water. My meal was so enjoyable and it was super filling. After stuffing my face with all falafel sandwich goodness my appetite was fully satisfied and I didn't feel like regret. Hahaha!!

Liba Falafel is a gem in the Uptown part of Oakland, wish they stayed open on weekends, but they do have a food truck which I hope is mobile on weekends. Liba is worth it and it makes you forget you're vegetarian for the moment,and if I was vegetarian I probably be eating Liba Falafel for the rest of my life in rotation with salads and peanut butter sandwiches.<//Text>

<Rate>4</Rate><review>4/22/13

THE CRUNCHY MUNCHY

So while I'm waiting in a long line in front of a different food truck, my eyes begin to wander to the truck next door which currently had no line. (Soon to change). I thought about switching lines to the falafels but my friends had finally decided on what they wanted in the first line so I just strolled over to get a closer look at the balls. Um, 1 for $1. Heck yes!

Me:                        One please.
Falafel truck dude: One sandwich?
Me.                        One falafel. Ball. ($1 in hand)
Falafel truck dude: Here you go - on the house!
Me:                        Sweeeeeeeeet

I got a free sample! Holy #$%& it was so good. It was a good size and didn't seem all that greasy (they can be so oily sometimes) and it was sooooo crunchy just like I like with a large layer of crunch.

I will absolutely order food from this truck next time I see them.<//review>< pics>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
Woo-hoo!  This neighborhood just keeps getting better.  If you like falafel, you're in for a treat.  Here's what's up:

You've probably seen the Liba Falafel food truck at farmer's markets and all around the bay area.  It's awesome.  They're known for super-crunchy falafel balls and a toppings bar full of gourmet and unexpected taste combos.

The storefront just opened a few months ago, and it's the same stuff.  Same owner.  Same ingredients.  Everyone is super nice and the storefront is really taking off.  The toppings bar rotates frequently and they also have great additions like almond horchata and some really great coconut chocolate patties.

You can either get a falafel sandwich or a falafel sandwich, either of which are to be generously supplemented with as much stuff from the toppings bar as you can get.  There are lots of sauces, including tzatziki and hummus, and things ranging from onions, to olives, to beets, to cabbage, to carrots, and everything in between.

The only thing I don't like about this place is the price.  It's a touch on the spendy side for a lunch, and the portions are a little underwhelming unless you really go ham on the toppings bar.  If a dollar or two were shaved off, I'd be happier.<//Review>

< text>
Probably the best Smog experience I have had, and I failed! Made an appointment online for my 1989 truck, another shop quoted $125+cert then dropped to $85 after I told them i had found a better deal, not how you win my business! $75+cert advertised price here. Pulled up at my appointment time as Sebastian was just finishing another car, perfect timing. He backed my truck onto the dyno, and told me to take a seat and relax, it would be about 20 mins. At around minute 35 i became a little worried, looked over and saw him under my car for quite a while. I later found out that my truck had passed every aspect of the test except, Sebastian couldn't read the CARB EO number on the catalytic converter because it had gotten rusted over probably due to a combo of salty air and leaking oil burning on it. This number was required to be input into the smog system for verification. Sebastian was under the car scrubbing, brushing, using chalk, shining light from all angles and he still couldn't get the last three digits. He took the time to explain this to me and said if I could get the numbers to show to bring it back and he would re-test for a nominal fee. When i got home i went to town on the metal with a wire wheel and a drill, and just barely got the numbers to show. Back to Advanced Smog in and out within 20 mins and a pass! Excellent customer service, fair price (even for pre 96 cars) and Sebastian is a cool dude who is easy to talk with, highly recommend this shop!< /text>

<userid>104005588180728437621</userid>< Review>
I love the trails here! First and for most the parking situation is much better compared to like the trails in Whittier-Hellmans Trail. It's next to a school and residential area.  So there is plenty of parking.  Currently the hours for the summer months are posted as 9am-6pm, but we're got there at 8:30 am and it was already open. There are plenty of trails to go of off.  You can go to the water tower and if you dare walk all the way to the Whittier tower.  There are great visit of the temple Buddhist temple on hacienda and of Rose Hills Mortuary.

It's a very scenic and some of the trails are naturally shaded which helps a lot.  The trails seem pretty clean.  So this is a friendly reminder to be aware of your trash.  Let's try not to ruin this piece of nature.... or anything at that matter.

I definitely recommend this trail!</Review>

< Review>
This is my to-go-to trail early in the morning I normally take the Coyote Trail up to Skyline Drive until reaching the Water Tower that‚Äôs my turning point. It‚Äôs a moderate trail but you definitely get your sweat going, after walking down the steep hill from the water tower I jog through Ahwingna Trail all the way until reaching 7th street. This circuit is 3.78mi I do want to try the other trails in Hacienda hills for an extra mile or two, you still have Puma trail, Native Oak Trail and thats just from this side of town there are other four trails that connect from Whittier too! It‚Äôs your pick and choose. These trails are kid friendly, some trails mountain bike accesible as well as horseback riding. The natural habitat really helps disconnecting you from everything and anything down back in the city,  really helpful nowadays with so much going on, very thankful to have these hills. Elevation is about 1,161ft, depending on the season you‚Äôll be seeing wildflowers there is poison Ivy you got to watch out for, also being a natural habitat there‚Äôs  mountain lions (which i‚Äôve yet to encounter), deer (I‚Äôve seen), coyotes, rattle snakes(nearly stepped on one!) just always be aware of tour surroundings at all time. But the views in a clear weather are the ones to breathe in and be thankful for. Blessings and just get out there and enjoy these trails!</Review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><text>Great hike in the middle of suburba! Right off the 60fwy and 7th. You take 7th and it ends at the trail head. Parking is limited inside (only 2 spots) but its across the street from a school and a side street with ample parking.
You start up a small incline on gravel then you hit pavement and it goes up hill at a decent incline.
If you take this hike and make lefts to loop. back around you will be at about 3 miles, but once you reach the water tower/summit you can take a number of other trails that can go for miles!
Usually well traveled to heavy congestion of people hiking, mountain biking, walkers, trail runners and the occasional yogis at each summit point.
Last time I went the grass was very tall about 5 ft (may 2019) but normally you get great views of the surrounding cities and on a clear day a view of DTLA
Hike is easy to moderate depending on your fitness level but it's very doable for anyone starting out or just wanting a quick workout</text>< Pics>

< review>
Betabrand used to be great, awesome even. Over the past year their quality control and customer service have tanked. Always try on the clothes you're buying. The sizing is different not just between different styles, but between every article. I've had to return clothes this year because they were not labeled correctly, yes, the sewn-in label was the incorrect size. Their return system sucks. They've disconnected their customer service phone line, and it took a month the for them to reply to an email the last time I had an issue with my order. It then took another 3 months to find a solution. In my last email I expressed how disappointed I was and how I didn't think I would be a  returning customer, which  they did not even bother to reply to. Their store has a dwindling supply of their clothes and the staff are generally useless since they don't know the products they're selling.
RIP Betabrand</review>

< Review>
Let's start off by saying, I will be back!! Mofongo's is a quaint Puerto Rican Restaurant. It was a hot day in the Valley but inside was so pleasantly chill not to cold but just right. I ordered the Passion Fruit tea (which is so delicious and they make it fresh daily) I got it Unsweetened but I'm sure Sweetened is just as thirst quenchingly delicious. On to the dinner, It was my first time here and not to mention my first time truly having Puerto Rican cuisine. The waiter was so nice and after mentioning the special of the day he also mentioned some of the other popular dishes and some personal choices. I went with the Monfongo Chicken Chicharrones with Plantains and it was absolutely delicious. The wait staff were so friendly and made sure you have/had a great meal. I love Monfongo's and I so recommend stoping by and trying the Passion Fruit tea and pick your favorite dish.</Review>

< review>
I have not been able to find any good Puerto Rican restaurant in LA until now (they're limited anyway, mostly Cuban). I happen to be near the area and found it on my search for food. Couldn't get more authentic than this.

The mofongo con carne guisado  was absolutely delicious. The meat was cooked perfectly and had great texture and flavor. If I had room for more I would've tried another one. More reason to make another trip to this restaurant soon.

The shrimp dish in their creole sauce was also very good. It had plenty of shrimp. The rice had very good flavoring and went well when I mixed in the shrimp.

Also, choose the tostones instead of the sweet cooked banana. They pair well with the Mofongo dishes.

Customer service was fantastic. Can't wait to come back to this place and try some other dishes. Happy I found this gem in NoHo.< /review>

<name>Steve Cha< /name><UserId.>113669553636359461479<//UserId.><text>Mofongos in North Hollywood was the first time I've tried Puerto Rican food of any kind. But what a great first impression Mofongos made. After hearing that it was so close to where I live and that they are the only full menu dine in Puerto Rican restaurant in Los Angeles, I knew I had to give it a shot. Of course, I ate the Mofongo dish. I got mine with the chicken stew and pork rinds, which was pretty awesome. I liked the flavor and the texture of the chicken stew on it. I also relleno de papa, their famous potato balls which were delicious and somewhat similar to the ones you can find at Porto's Bakery. Their alcapurrias yucca fritters were amazing. I'd come back here again just for this one! And I ended it off well with the tembleque, which is the coconut pudding dessert! It had that panna cotta texture with an amazing coconut flavor and flakes that makes it a must try.

I definitely recommend Mofongo's if you want to try some great Puerto Rican food. The parking here is great, especially since there is so much street parking. It's a small restaurant, but it really has a cool Puerto Rico, coastal vibe inside of it. You feel like you're transported to that island. I shot a YouTube video of my experience here, which you can find on my YouTube channel called Rockstar Eater.< /text></record></dataset><record>

<rate>3<//rate>< Text>
I was happy to find Hispanic food from the islands in LA. I'm a recent transplant from the east coast and have been missing it. The menu has many PR food staples: mofongo (of course), arroz con habichuelas, tostones, bacalaitos, bistec, a bunch of frituras... pastelitos!

Part of me does see the menu as limited, however, especially since I no longer eat meat (I do eat fish) or dairy so if you have dietary restrictions, you may not be as excited about the menu.

I got tostones and arroz con habichuelas to-go... The taste was fine ü§∑üèΩ‚Äç‚ôÄÔ∏è I wanted to get some a couple pastelitos for a friend but they only sold them in groups of four which would have cost too much. Maybe I'm comparing it too much to Boston, but you'd be able to buy them individually there :( Jury is still out on taste/flavors but I think they deserve a second chance.</Text>

< rating>
3<//rating>
< Text>
Came to eat here with some friends, one of whom is Puerto Rican, and recommended this place. It is pretty lowkey and small. We ordered the pastel de pollo, which is like a tamal but made with banana and wrapped on a banana leaf. My friends really seemed to enjoy it, but it wasn't for me, the cooked plantain flavor and texture was a bit overwhelming for me, but the filling was good, but too little. For the main course I had the mofongo with pork, which was tasty, but a bit bland for my taste. The pork was similar to carnitas but crispier and not as flavorful. I accidentally ordered the tostones to accompany this, which didn't have much flavor for me, I had meant to get the cooked plantain which is sweeter. I would say that my favorite part was the rice, which was delicious and had a homemade taste to it. I do have to add, that we had ordered a cortadito and a sangria before dinner, which we never received.< /Text>

The restuarant is cute but staff is careless.< /Review>
